<p><span style="font-size: small;"><span id="coordinates"><a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">Coordinates</a>: <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Nuremberg_trials&amp;params=49_27.2603_N_11_02.9103_E_region:DE_type:event"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">49°27.2603′N</span> <span class="longitude">11°02.9103′E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">49.4543383°N 11.0485050°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">49.4543383; 11.0485050</span></span></span></a></span></span></span> The <b>Nuremberg trials</b> (German: <i>die Nürnberger Prozesse</i>) were a series of <a href="/wiki/Military_tribunal" class="mw-redirect" title="Military tribunal">military tribunals</a> held by the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied forces</a> under <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Laws_of_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Laws of war">laws of war</a> after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. The trials were most notable for the prosecution of prominent members of the political, military, judicial and economic leadership of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>, who planned, carried out, or otherwise participated in <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">the Holocaust</a> and other <a href="/wiki/War_crimes" class="mw-redirect" title="War crimes">war crimes</a>. The trials were held in the city of <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg" title="Nuremberg">Nuremberg</a>, Germany, and their decisions marked a turning point between classical and contemporary international law.</p>
<p>The first and best known set of these trials were those of the major war criminals before the <a href="/wiki/International_Military_Tribunal" class="mw-redirect" title="International Military Tribunal">International Military Tribunal</a> (IMT). They were described as "the greatest trial in history" by <a href="/wiki/Norman_Birkett,_1st_Baron_Birkett" title="Norman Birkett, 1st Baron Birkett">Norman Birkett</a>, one of the British judges who presided over them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrus1997.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fwww.jstor.org.2Fstable.2F41212687_563.5D_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrus1997.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fwww.jstor.org.2Fstable.2F41212687_563.5D-1">[1]</a></sup> Held between 20 November 1945 and 1 October 1946,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris2006.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3D5h_8dxXEIPsC.26pg.3DPA106.26dq.3D.2522november.2B20.2B1945.2522.2B.2522october.2B1.2B1946.2522_106.5D_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris2006.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3D5h_8dxXEIPsC.26pg.3DPA106.26dq.3D.2522november.2B20.2B1945.2522.2B.2522october.2B1.2B1946.2522_106.5D-2">[2]</a></sup> the Tribunal was given the task of trying 24 of the most important political and military leaders of the Third Reich – though the proceedings of <a href="/wiki/Martin_Bormann" title="Martin Bormann">Martin Bormann</a> was <a href="/wiki/Trial_in_absentia" title="Trial in absentia">tried <i>in absentia</i></a>, while another, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Ley" title="Robert Ley">Robert Ley</a>, committed <a href="/wiki/Suicide" title="Suicide">suicide</a> within a week of the trial's commencement.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Himmler" title="Heinrich Himmler">Heinrich Himmler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Burgdorf" title="Wilhelm Burgdorf">Wilhelm Burgdorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hans_Krebs_(Wehrmacht_general)" title="Hans Krebs (Wehrmacht general)">Hans Krebs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Goebbels" title="Joseph Goebbels">Joseph Goebbels</a> had all committed suicide in the spring of 1945 to avoid capture, though Himmler was captured before his suicide and Krebs and Burgdorf committed suicide two days after <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Adolf_Hitler" title="Death of Adolf Hitler">that of Hitler's</a> in the <a href="/wiki/F%C3%BChrerbunker" title="Führerbunker">same place</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Reinhard_Heydrich" title="Reinhard Heydrich">Reinhard Heydrich</a> had been <a href="/wiki/Operation_Anthropoid" title="Operation Anthropoid">assassinated by Czech partisans in 1942</a>, so he was not included. <a href="/wiki/Josef_Terboven" title="Josef Terboven">Josef Terboven</a> killed himself with dynamite in the <a href="/wiki/F%C3%BChrerbunker" title="Führerbunker">Führerbunker</a> in 1945. <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Eichmann" title="Adolf Eichmann">Adolf Eichmann</a> fled to <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> to avoid Allied capture, but was captured by Israel's intelligence service the <a href="/wiki/Mossad" title="Mossad">Mossad</a>, convicted of war crimes, and hanged in 1962. <a href="/wiki/Hermann_G%C3%B6ring" title="Hermann Göring">Hermann Göring</a> was sentenced to death but committed suicide the night before his execution as a perceived act of defiance against his captors. <a href="/wiki/Mikl%C3%B3s_Horthy" title="Miklós Horthy">Miklós Horthy</a> appeared as a witness at the <a href="/wiki/Ministries_trial" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministries trial">Ministries trial</a> held in Nuremberg in 1948.</p>
<p>This article primarily deals with the first set of trials conducted by the IMT. A second set of trials of lesser war criminals was conducted under Control Council Law No. 10 at the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Subsequent_Nuremberg_trials" title="Subsequent Nuremberg trials">Nuremberg Military Tribunal (NMT)</a>, which included the <a href="/wiki/Doctors%27_trial" title="Doctors' trial">Doctors' trial</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Judges%27_Trial" title="Judges' Trial">Judges' Trial</a>.</p>
<p>The typification of the crimes and the constitution of the court represented a juridical advance that would be used afterwards by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> for the development of a specific international jurisprudence in matter of <a href="/wiki/War_crime" title="War crime">war crime</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">crimes against humanity</a>, <a href="/wiki/War_of_aggression" title="War of aggression">war of aggression</a>, as well as for the creation of the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origin">Origin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg_trials&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Origin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:30%; padding: 10px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>There were, I suppose, three possible courses: to let the atrocities which had been committed go unpunished; to put the perpetrators to death or punish them by executive action; or to try them. Which was it to be? Was it possible to let such atrocities go unpunished? Could France, could Russia, could Holland, Belgium, Norway, Czechoslovakia, Poland or Yugoslavia be expected to consent to such a course?&#160;... It will be remembered that after the First World War alleged criminals were handed over to be <a href="/wiki/Leipzig_War_Crimes_Trials" title="Leipzig War Crimes Trials">tried by Germany</a>, and what a farce that was! The majority got off and such sentences as were inflicted were derisory and were soon remitted.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left; text-align: right;">—<a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Lawrence,_1st_Baron_Oaksey" title="Geoffrey Lawrence, 1st Baron Oaksey">Geoffrey Lawrence</a><br />
5 December 1946</cite></div>
<p>A&#160;precedent for trying those accused of <a href="/wiki/War_crime" title="War crime">war crimes</a> had been set at the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Leipzig_War_Crimes_Trials" title="Leipzig War Crimes Trials">Leipzig War Crimes Trials</a> held in May to July 1921 before the <i><a href="/wiki/Reichsgericht" title="Reichsgericht">Reichsgericht</a></i> (German Supreme Court) in <a href="/wiki/Leipzig" title="Leipzig">Leipzig</a>, although these had been on a very limited scale and largely regarded as ineffectual. At the beginning of 1940, the Polish government-in-exile asked the British and French governments to condemn the German invasion of their country. The British initially declined to do so; however, in April 1940, a joint declaration was issued by the British, French and Polish. Relatively bland because of Anglo-French reservations, it proclaimed the trio's <i>"desire to make a formal and public protest to the conscience of the world against the action of the German government whom they must hold responsible for these crimes which cannot remain unpunished."</i><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKochavi1998.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DQGi1kxDF-30C.26pg.3DPA7.26dq.3D.2522beginning.2Bof.2B1940.2522_7.E2.80.938.5D_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKochavi1998.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DQGi1kxDF-30C.26pg.3DPA7.26dq.3D.2522beginning.2Bof.2B1940.2522_7.E2.80.938.5D-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>Three-and-a-half years later, the stated intention to punish the Germans was much more trenchant. On 1 November 1943, the Soviet Union, the United Kingdom and the United States published their <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Declaration" class="mw-redirect" title="Moscow Declaration">"Declaration on German Atrocities in Occupied Europe"</a>, which gave a "full warning" that, when the Nazis were defeated, the Allies would "pursue them to the uttermost ends of the earth&#160;... in order that justice may be done.&#160;... The above declaration is without prejudice to the case of the major war criminals whose offences have no particular geographical location and who will be punished by a joint decision of the Government of the Allies."<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> This intention by the Allies to dispense justice was reiterated at the <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">Yalta Conference</a> and at <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> in 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWright194674_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWright194674-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>British <a href="/wiki/War_Cabinet" class="mw-redirect" title="War Cabinet">War Cabinet</a> documents, released on 2 January 2006, showed that as early as December 1944 the Cabinet had discussed their policy for the punishment of the leading Nazis if captured. The <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">British Prime Minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>, had then advocated a policy of <a href="/wiki/Summary_execution" title="Summary execution">summary execution</a> in some circumstances, with the use of an <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Attainder" class="mw-redirect" title="Act of Attainder">Act of Attainder</a> to circumvent legal obstacles, being dissuaded from this only by talks with US and Soviet leaders later in the war.<sup id="cite_ref-AD042113_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AD042113-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nuremberg_Trials_retouched.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Nuremberg_Trials_retouched.jpg/220px-Nuremberg_Trials_retouched.jpg" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Nuremberg_Trials_retouched.jpg/330px-Nuremberg_Trials_retouched.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Nuremberg_Trials_retouched.jpg/440px-Nuremberg_Trials_retouched.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2931" data-file-height="2259" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nuremberg_Trials_retouched.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Defendants in the dock at the Nuremberg trials. The main target of the prosecution was <a href="/wiki/Hermann_G%C3%B6ring" title="Hermann Göring">Hermann Göring</a> (at the left edge on the first row of benches), considered to be the most important surviving official in the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Third <i>Reich</i></a> after Hitler's death.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In late 1943, during the Tripartite Dinner Meeting at the <a href="/wiki/Tehran_Conference" title="Tehran Conference">Tehran Conference</a>, the Soviet leader, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a>, proposed executing 50,000–100,000 German staff officers. <a href="/wiki/US_President" class="mw-redirect" title="US President">US President</a> <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> joked that perhaps 49,000 would do. Churchill, believing them to be serious, denounced the idea of "the cold blooded execution of soldiers who fought for their country" and that he would rather be "taken out in the courtyard and shot" himself than partake in any such action.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESenarclens1988.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DsbAo3RkWIUsC.26pg.3DPA19_pp._19.E2.80.9320.5D_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESenarclens1988.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DsbAo3RkWIUsC.26pg.3DPA19_pp._19.E2.80.9320.5D-9">[9]</a></sup> However, he also stated that war criminals must pay for their crimes and that, in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Declaration#Statement_on_Atrocities" class="mw-redirect" title="Moscow Declaration">Moscow Document</a> which he himself had written, they should be tried at the places where the crimes were committed. Churchill was vigorously opposed to executions "for political purposes."<sup id="cite_ref-Churchill:_execute_Hitler_without_trial_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Churchill:_execute_Hitler_without_trial-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-teachingamericanhistory_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teachingamericanhistory-11">[11]</a></sup> According to the minutes of a meeting between Roosevelt and Stalin at Yalta, on 4 February 1945, at the <a href="/wiki/Livadia_Palace" title="Livadia Palace">Livadia Palace</a>, President Roosevelt "said that he had been very much struck by the extent of German destruction in the <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimea</a> and therefore he was more bloodthirsty in regard to the Germans than he had been a year ago, and he hoped that Marshal Stalin would again propose a toast to the execution of 50,000 officers of the <a href="/wiki/German_Army_(Wehrmacht)" title="German Army (Wehrmacht)">German Army</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-wisc_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wisc-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Henry_Morgenthau_Jr." title="Henry Morgenthau Jr.">Henry Morgenthau Jr.</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_the_Treasury" title="United States Secretary of the Treasury">US Secretary of the Treasury</a>, suggested a plan for the total <a href="/wiki/Denazification" title="Denazification">denazification</a> of Germany;<sup id="cite_ref-marist_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marist-13">[13]</a></sup> this was known as the <a href="/wiki/Morgenthau_Plan" title="Morgenthau Plan">Morgenthau Plan</a>. The plan advocated the forced de-industrialisation of Germany and the summary execution of so-called "arch-criminals", i.e. the major war criminals.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Roosevelt initially supported this plan, and managed to convince Churchill to support it in a less drastic form. Later, details were leaked generating widespread condemnation by the nation's newspapers. Roosevelt, aware of strong public disapproval, abandoned the plan, but did not adopt an alternative position on the matter. The demise of the Morgenthau Plan created the need for an alternative method of dealing with the Nazi leadership. The plan for the "Trial of European War Criminals" was drafted by <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_War" title="United States Secretary of War">Secretary of War</a> <a href="/wiki/Henry_L._Stimson" title="Henry L. Stimson">Henry L. Stimson</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_War" title="United States Department of War">War Department</a>. Following Roosevelt's death in April 1945, the new president, <a href="/wiki/Harry_S._Truman" title="Harry S. Truman">Harry S. Truman</a>, gave strong approval for a judicial process. After a series of negotiations between Britain, the US, Soviet Union and France, details of the trial were worked out. The trials were to commence on 20 November 1945, in the <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavarian</a> city of Nuremberg.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Creation_of_the_courts">Creation of the courts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg_trials&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Creation of the courts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On 20 April 1942, representatives from the nine countries occupied by Germany met in London to draft the "Inter-Allied Resolution on German War Crimes". At the meetings in <a href="/wiki/Tehran_Conference" title="Tehran Conference">Tehran</a> (1943), <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">Yalta</a> (1945) and <a href="/wiki/Potsdam_Conference" title="Potsdam Conference">Potsdam</a> (1945), the three major wartime powers, the United Kingdom, United States, and the Soviet Union, agreed on the format of punishment for those responsible for war crimes during World War II. France was also awarded a place on the tribunal. The legal basis for the trial was established by the <a href="/wiki/London_Charter_of_the_International_Military_Tribunal" class="mw-redirect" title="London Charter of the International Military Tribunal">London Charter</a>, which was agreed upon by the four so-called Great Powers on 8 August 1945, <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELawrence1947.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fwww.jstor.org.2Fstable.2F3018884_151.5D_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELawrence1947.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fwww.jstor.org.2Fstable.2F3018884_151.5D-15">[15]</a></sup> and which restricted the trial to "punishment of the major war criminals of the European Axis countries"</p>
<p>Some 200 German war crimes defendants were tried at Nuremberg, and 1,600 others were tried under the traditional channels of military justice. The legal basis for the jurisdiction of the court was that defined by the <a href="/wiki/German_Instrument_of_Surrender,_1945" class="mw-redirect" title="German Instrument of Surrender, 1945">Instrument of Surrender of Germany</a>. Political authority for Germany had been transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Allied_Control_Council" title="Allied Control Council">Allied Control Council</a> which, having sovereign power over Germany, could choose to punish violations of <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Laws_of_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Laws of war">laws of war</a>. Because the court was limited to violations of the laws of war, it did not have jurisdiction over crimes that took place before the outbreak of war on 1 September 1939.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Location">Location</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg_trials&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Location">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ostbau_Justizpalast_N%C3%BCrnberg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Ostbau_Justizpalast_N%C3%BCrnberg.jpg/220px-Ostbau_Justizpalast_N%C3%BCrnberg.jpg" width="220" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Ostbau_Justizpalast_N%C3%BCrnberg.jpg/330px-Ostbau_Justizpalast_N%C3%BCrnberg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Ostbau_Justizpalast_N%C3%BCrnberg.jpg/440px-Ostbau_Justizpalast_N%C3%BCrnberg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="929" data-file-height="457" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ostbau_Justizpalast_N%C3%BCrnberg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The courthouse in Nuremberg, where the trials took place</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Leipzig" title="Leipzig">Leipzig</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a> were briefly considered as the location for the trial.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOvery200119.E2.80.9320_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOvery200119.E2.80.9320-16">[16]</a></sup> The Soviet Union had wanted the trials to take place in Berlin, as the capital city of the 'fascist conspirators',<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOvery200119.E2.80.9320_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOvery200119.E2.80.9320-16">[16]</a></sup> but Nuremberg was chosen as the site for two reasons, with the first one having been the decisive factor:<sup id="cite_ref-Catalogue1_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catalogue1-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<ol>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Justice_(Nuremberg)" class="mw-redirect" title="Palace of Justice (Nuremberg)">Palace of Justice</a> was spacious and largely undamaged (one of the few buildings that had remained largely intact through extensive Allied bombing of Germany), and a large prison was also part of the complex.</li>
<li>Nuremberg was considered the ceremonial birthplace of the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a>. It had hosted the Party's annual <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_rallies" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuremberg rallies">propaganda rallies</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOvery200119.E2.80.9320_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOvery200119.E2.80.9320-16">[16]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Reichstag_(Nazi_Germany)" title="Reichstag (Nazi Germany)">Reichstag</a> session that passed the <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Laws" title="Nuremberg Laws">Nuremberg Laws</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Catalogue1_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catalogue1-17">[17]</a></sup> Thus it was considered a fitting place to mark the Party's symbolic demise.</li>
</ol>
<p>As a compromise with the Soviets, it was agreed that while the location of the trial would be Nuremberg, Berlin would be the official home of the Tribunal authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-heydecker-leeb_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heydecker-leeb-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PRO-LCO-2.2F2980-1_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PRO-LCO-2.2F2980-1-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PRO-LCO-2.2F2980-2_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PRO-LCO-2.2F2980-2-20">[20]</a></sup> It was also agreed that France would become the permanent seat of the IMT<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOvery200115_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOvery200115-21">[21]</a></sup> and that the first trial (several were planned) would take place in Nuremberg.<sup id="cite_ref-heydecker-leeb_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heydecker-leeb-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PRO-LCO-2.2F2980-2_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PRO-LCO-2.2F2980-2-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most of the accused had previously been detained at <a href="/wiki/Camp_Ashcan" title="Camp Ashcan">Camp Ashcan</a>, a processing station and interrogation center in Luxembourg, and were moved to Nuremberg for the trial.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Participants">Participants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg_trials&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Participants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Each of the four countries provided one judge and an alternative, as well as a prosecutor.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:View_of_judges_panel_during_testimony_Nuremberg_Trials_1945.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/View_of_judges_panel_during_testimony_Nuremberg_Trials_1945.jpeg/220px-View_of_judges_panel_during_testimony_Nuremberg_Trials_1945.jpeg" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/View_of_judges_panel_during_testimony_Nuremberg_Trials_1945.jpeg/330px-View_of_judges_panel_during_testimony_Nuremberg_Trials_1945.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/View_of_judges_panel_during_testimony_Nuremberg_Trials_1945.jpeg/440px-View_of_judges_panel_during_testimony_Nuremberg_Trials_1945.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1001" data-file-height="808" /></a>

Judges sitting in Nuremberg, from left to right: <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Volchkov" title="Alexander Volchkov">Volchkov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iona_Nikitchenko" title="Iona Nikitchenko">Nikitchenko</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norman_Birkett,_1st_Baron_Birkett" title="Norman Birkett, 1st Baron Birkett">Birkett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Lawrence,_1st_Baron_Oaksey" title="Geoffrey Lawrence, 1st Baron Oaksey">Sir Geoffrey Lawrence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francis_Biddle" title="Francis Biddle">Biddle</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_J._Parker" title="John J. Parker">Parker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henri_Donnedieu_de_Vabres" title="Henri Donnedieu de Vabres">Donnedieu de Vabres</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Falco" title="Robert Falco">Falco</a></div>
</div>
</div>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Chief_prosecutors">Chief prosecutors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg_trials&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Chief prosecutors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom"><img alt="United Kingdom" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Attorney_General_for_England_and_Wales" title="Attorney General for England and Wales">Attorney General</a> <a href="/wiki/Hartley_Shawcross,_Baron_Shawcross" class="mw-redirect" title="Hartley Shawcross, Baron Shawcross">Sir Hartley Shawcross</a> (United Kingdom)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Flag_of_the_United_States_%281912-1959%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States_%281912-1959%29.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Flag_of_the_United_States_%281912-1959%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States_%281912-1959%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Flag_of_the_United_States_%281912-1959%29.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States_%281912-1959%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1900" data-file-height="1000" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_Justice" class="mw-redirect" title="Supreme Court Justice">Supreme Court Justice</a> <a href="/wiki/Robert_H._Jackson" title="Robert H. Jackson">Robert H. Jackson</a> (United States)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union"><img alt="Soviet Union" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union_%281936-1955%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union_%281936-1955%29.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union_%281936-1955%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union_%281936-1955%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union_%281936-1955%29.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union_%281936-1955%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="300" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant-General" class="mw-redirect" title="Lieutenant-General">Lieutenant-General</a> <a href="/wiki/Roman_Rudenko" title="Roman Rudenko">Roman Andreyevich Rudenko</a> (Soviet Union)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/French_Fourth_Republic" title="French Fourth Republic"><img alt="French Fourth Republic" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Menthon" title="François de Menthon">François de Menthon</a>, later replaced by <a href="/wiki/Auguste_Champetier_de_Ribes" title="Auguste Champetier de Ribes">Auguste Champetier de Ribes</a> (France)</li>
</ul>
<p>Assisting Jackson were the lawyers <a href="/wiki/Telford_Taylor" title="Telford Taylor">Telford Taylor</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> William S. Kaplan<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_J._Dodd" title="Thomas J. Dodd">Thomas J. Dodd</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Sonnenfeldt" title="Richard Sonnenfeldt">Richard Sonnenfeldt</a>, a <a href="/wiki/US_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="US Army">US Army</a> <a href="/wiki/Interpreter" class="mw-redirect" title="Interpreter">interpreter</a>. Assisting Shawcross were <a href="/wiki/Major" title="Major">Major</a> <a href="/wiki/David_Maxwell_Fyfe,_1st_Earl_of_Kilmuir" title="David Maxwell Fyfe, 1st Earl of Kilmuir">Sir David Maxwell-Fyfe</a> and Sir <a href="/wiki/John_Wheeler-Bennett" title="John Wheeler-Bennett">John Wheeler-Bennett</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mervyn_Griffith-Jones" title="Mervyn Griffith-Jones">Mervyn Griffith-Jones</a>, who was later to become famous as the chief prosecutor in the <i><a href="/wiki/Lady_Chatterley%27s_Lover" title="Lady Chatterley's Lover">Lady Chatterley's Lover</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Obscenity" title="Obscenity">obscenity</a> trial, was also on Shawcross's team. Shawcross also recruited a young <a href="/wiki/Barrister" title="Barrister">barrister</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Marreco" title="Anthony Marreco">Anthony Marreco</a>, who was the son of a friend of his, to help the British team with the heavy workload.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Defense_counsel">Defense counsel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg_trials&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Defense counsel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The vast majority of the <a href="/wiki/Defense_attorney" class="mw-redirect" title="Defense attorney">defense attorneys</a> were German lawyers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavidson1997.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DkN-mc0QxyhYC.26pg.3DPA30_30.E2.80.931.5D_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavidson1997.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DkN-mc0QxyhYC.26pg.3DPA30_30.E2.80.931.5D-24">[24]</a></sup> These included Georg Fröschmann, Heinz Fritz (Hans Fritzsche), <a href="/wiki/Otto_Kranzb%C3%BChler" title="Otto Kranzbühler">Otto Kranzbühler</a> (Karl Dönitz), Otto Pannenbecker (Wilhelm Frick), Alfred Thoma (Alfred Rosenberg), Kurt Kauffmann (Ernst Kaltenbrunner), Hans Laternser (general staff and high command), Franz Exner (Alfred Jodl), Alfred Seidl (Hans Frank), Otto Stahmer (Hermann Göring), Walter Ballas (Gustav Krupp von Bohlen und Halbach), Hans Flächsner (Albert Speer), Günther von Rohrscheidt (Rudolf Heß), Egon Kubuschok (Franz von Papen), <a href="/wiki/Robert_Servatius" title="Robert Servatius">Robert Servatius</a> (Fritz Sauckel), Fritz Sauter (Joachim von Ribbentrop), Walther Funk (Baldur von Schirach), Hanns Marx (Julius Streicher), Otto Nelte (Wilhelm Keitel), and Herbert Kraus / Rudolph Dix (both working for Hjalmar Schacht). The main counsels were supported by a total of 70 assistants, clerks and lawyers.<sup id="cite_ref-Catalogue3_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catalogue3-25">[25]</a></sup> The defense counsel witnesses included several men who took part in the war crimes during World War II, such as <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_H%C3%B6ss" title="Rudolf Höss">Rudolf Höss</a>. The men testifying for the defense hoped to receive more lenient sentences.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (March 2013)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> All of the men testifying on behalf of the defense were found guilty on several counts.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Trial">Trial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg_trials&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Trial">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Defendants_in_the_dock_at_nuremberg_trials.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Defendants_in_the_dock_at_nuremberg_trials.jpg/220px-Defendants_in_the_dock_at_nuremberg_trials.jpg" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Defendants_in_the_dock_at_nuremberg_trials.jpg/330px-Defendants_in_the_dock_at_nuremberg_trials.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Defendants_in_the_dock_at_nuremberg_trials.jpg/440px-Defendants_in_the_dock_at_nuremberg_trials.jpg 2x" data-file-width="761" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Defendants_in_the_dock_at_nuremberg_trials.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rare color photo of the trial at Nuremberg, depicting the defendants, guarded by American Military Police</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The International Military Tribunal was opened on 19 November 1945 in the Palace of Justice in Nuremberg.<sup id="cite_ref-Catalogue2_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catalogue2-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-indictment_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indictment-28">[28]</a></sup> The first session was presided over by the Soviet judge, Nikitchenko. The prosecution entered indictments against 24 major war criminals and seven organizations – the leadership of the <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazi</a> party, the Reich Cabinet, the <a href="/wiki/Schutzstaffel" title="Schutzstaffel">Schutzstaffel</a> (SS), <a href="/wiki/Sicherheitsdienst" title="Sicherheitsdienst">Sicherheitsdienst</a> (SD), the <a href="/wiki/Gestapo" title="Gestapo">Gestapo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sturmabteilung" title="Sturmabteilung">Sturmabteilung</a> (SA) and the "General Staff and High Command", comprising several categories of senior military officers.<sup id="cite_ref-IMT_Appendix_B_group.3Davalon_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMT_Appendix_B_group.3Davalon-29">[avalon 1]</a></sup> These organizations were to be declared "criminal" if found guilty.</p>
<p>The indictments were for:</p>
<ol>
<li>Participation in a <a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_(crime)" class="mw-redirect" title="Conspiracy (crime)">common plan or conspiracy</a> for the accomplishment of a <a href="/wiki/Crime_against_peace" title="Crime against peace">crime against peace</a></li>
<li>Planning, initiating and waging <a href="/wiki/War_of_aggression" title="War of aggression">wars of aggression</a> and other crimes against peace</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/War_crime" title="War crime">War crimes</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Crime_against_humanity" class="mw-redirect" title="Crime against humanity">Crimes against humanity</a></li>
</ol>
<p>The 24 accused were, with respect to each charge, either <a href="/wiki/Indictment" title="Indictment">indicted</a> but not convicted (I), indicted and found guilty (G), or not charged (—), as listed below by defendant, charge, and eventual outcome:</p>

<td>Leader of the <i><a href="/wiki/Kriegsmarine" title="Kriegsmarine">Kriegsmarine</a></i> from 1943, succeeded Raeder. Initiator of the <a href="/wiki/U-boat" title="U-boat">U-boat</a> campaign. Briefly became <a href="/wiki/President_of_Germany" title="President of Germany">President of Germany</a> following Hitler's death.<sup id="cite_ref-donitz_group.3Davalon_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-donitz_group.3Davalon-31">[avalon 3]</a></sup> Convicted of carrying out <a href="/wiki/Unrestricted_submarine_warfare" title="Unrestricted submarine warfare">unrestricted submarine warfare</a> in breach of the 1936 <a href="/wiki/Second_London_Naval_Treaty" title="Second London Naval Treaty">Second London Naval Treaty</a>, but was not punished for that charge because <a href="/wiki/Chester_W._Nimitz#Post_war" title="Chester W. Nimitz">the United States committed the same breach</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NT_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NT-32">[29]</a></sup> Released 1 October 1956. Died 24 December 1980. Defense attorney: <a href="/wiki/Otto_Kranzb%C3%BChler" title="Otto Kranzbühler">Otto Kranzbühler</a></td>

<td data-sort-value="99">Death</td>
<td><i><a href="/wiki/Reichsmarschall" title="Reichsmarschall">Reichsmarschall</a></i>, Commander of the <i><a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a></i> 1935–45, Chief of the 4-Year Plan 1936–45, and original head of the <a href="/wiki/Gestapo" title="Gestapo">Gestapo</a> before turning it over to the <a href="/wiki/SS" class="mw-redirect" title="SS">SS</a> in April 1934. Originally the second-highest-ranked member of the Nazi Party and Hitler's designated successor, he fell out of favor with Hitler in April 1945. Highest ranking Nazi official to be tried at Nuremberg. <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2008509.2C_724_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2008509.2C_724-39">[32]</a></sup> Committed suicide the night before his execution.<sup id="cite_ref-Goering_judgement_group.3Davalon_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Goering_judgement_group.3Davalon-40">[avalon 8]</a></sup></td>

<td>Hitler's Deputy Führer until he flew to Scotland in 1941 in an attempt to broker peace with the United Kingdom. Had been imprisoned since then. After trial, incarcerated at <a href="/wiki/Spandau_Prison" title="Spandau Prison">Spandau Prison</a>, where he committed suicide in 1987.<sup id="cite_ref-Hess_judgement_group.3Davalon_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hess_judgement_group.3Davalon-41">[avalon 9]</a></sup></td>

<td><i><a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">Wehrmacht</a></i> <i><a href="/wiki/Generaloberst" class="mw-redirect" title="Generaloberst">Generaloberst</a></i>, Keitel's subordinate and Chief of the OKW's Operations Division 1938–45. Signed orders for the summary execution of Allied commandos and Soviet commissars <sup id="cite_ref-Jodl_judgement_group.3Davalon_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jodl_judgement_group.3Davalon-42">[avalon 10]</a></sup> Signed <a href="/wiki/German_Instrument_of_Surrender" title="German Instrument of Surrender">the instruments of surrender</a> on 7 May 1945 in Reims as the representative of <a href="/wiki/Karl_D%C3%B6nitz" title="Karl Dönitz">Karl Dönitz</a>. Hanged 16 October 1946. Posthumously rehabilitated in 1953, which was later reversed.</td>

<td data-sort-value="99">Death</td>
<td>Head of <a href="/wiki/Oberkommando_der_Wehrmacht" title="Oberkommando der Wehrmacht">Oberkommando der Wehrmacht</a> (OKW) and de facto defence minister 1938–45. Known for his unquestioning loyalty to Hitler.<sup id="cite_ref-Catalogue6_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catalogue6-44">[33]</a></sup> Signed numerous orders calling for soldiers and political prisoners to be executed. Expressed repentance.<sup id="cite_ref-Keitel_judgement_group.3Davalon_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keitel_judgement_group.3Davalon-45">[avalon 12]</a></sup> Hanged 16 October 1946.</td>

<td data-sort-value="Krupp, Gustav"><a href="/wiki/Gustav_Krupp_von_Bohlen_und_Halbach" title="Gustav Krupp von Bohlen und Halbach">Gustav Krupp von Bohlen und Halbach</a></td>
<td>&#160;</td>
<td>I</td>
<td>I</td>
<td>I</td>
<td data-sort-value="1">No decision</td>
<td>Major industrialist. C.E.O. of <a href="/wiki/Krupp" title="Krupp">Friedrich Krupp AG</a> 1912–45. Medically unfit for trial; he had been partially paralyzed since 1941. Due to an error, Gustav, instead of his son <a href="/wiki/Alfried_Krupp_von_Bohlen_und_Halbach" title="Alfried Krupp von Bohlen und Halbach">Alfried</a> (who ran Krupp for his father during most of the war), was selected for indictment.<sup id="cite_ref-Catalogue7_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catalogue7-46">[34]</a></sup> The prosecutors attempted to substitute his son in the indictment, but the judges rejected this due to proximity to trial. However, the charges against him remained on record in the event he should recover (he died in February 1950).<sup id="cite_ref-From_Nuremberg_to_the_Hague_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-From_Nuremberg_to_the_Hague-47">[35]</a></sup> Alfried was tried in a separate Nuremberg trial (the <a href="/wiki/Krupp_Trial" title="Krupp Trial">Krupp Trial</a>) for the use of slave labour, thereby escaping worse charges and possible execution.</td>
</tr>

<td>Head of <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Arbeitsfront" class="mw-redirect" title="Deutsche Arbeitsfront">DAF</a>, German Labour Front. Committed suicide on 25 October 1945, before the trial began. Indicted but neither acquitted nor found guilty as trial did not proceed.</td>

<td data-sort-value="15">15 years</td>
<td>Minister of Foreign Affairs 1932–38, succeeded by Ribbentrop. Later, Protector of <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moravia" title="Moravia">Moravia</a> 1939–43. On furlough since 1941, he resigned in 1943 because of a dispute with Hitler. Released (ill health) 6 November 1954<sup id="cite_ref-Von_Neurath_judgement_group.3Davalon_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Von_Neurath_judgement_group.3Davalon-48">[avalon 13]</a></sup> after suffering a heart attack. Died 14 August 1956.</td>

<td>—</td>
<td>—</td>
<td data-sort-value="0">Acquitted</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Chancellor" title="Chancellor">Chancellor of Germany</a> in 1932 and Vice-Chancellor under Hitler in 1933–34. Ambassador to Austria 1934–38 and ambassador to <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> 1939–44. Although acquitted at Nuremberg, von Papen was reclassified as a war criminal in 1947 by a German de-Nazification court, and sentenced to eight years' hard labour. He was acquitted following appeal after serving two years.<sup id="cite_ref-Von_Papen_judgement_group.3Davalon_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Von_Papen_judgement_group.3Davalon-49">[avalon 14]</a></sup></td>

<td data-sort-value="0">Acquitted</td>
<td>Prominent banker and economist. Pre-war president of the <i>Reichsbank</i> 1923–30 &amp; 1933–38 and Economics Minister 1934–37. Admitted to violating the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Schacht_judgement_group.3Davalon_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schacht_judgement_group.3Davalon-54">[avalon 19]</a></sup> Many at Nuremberg alleged that the British had brought about Schacht's acquittal to safeguard German industrialists and financiers; <a href="/wiki/Francis_Biddle" title="Francis Biddle">Francis Biddle</a> revealed <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Lawrence,_1st_Baron_Oaksey" title="Geoffrey Lawrence, 1st Baron Oaksey">Geoffrey Lawrence</a> had argued that Schacht, being a "man of character", was nothing like the other "ruffians" on trial.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBower1995347_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBower1995347-55">[36]</a></sup> By 1944, he had been imprisoned in a concentration camp by the Nazis, and was outraged to be put on trial as a major war criminal.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[37]</a></sup></td>
</tr>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Intelligence_tests_and_psychiatric_assessments">Intelligence tests and psychiatric assessments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg_trials&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Intelligence tests and psychiatric assessments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rorschach_test" title="Rorschach test">Rorschach test</a> was administered to the defendants, along with the <a href="/wiki/Thematic_Apperception_Test" class="mw-redirect" title="Thematic Apperception Test">Thematic Apperception Test</a> and a German adaptation of the <a href="/wiki/Wechsler_Adult_Intelligence_Scale" title="Wechsler Adult Intelligence Scale">Wechsler-Bellevue Intelligence Test</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrunner2001234_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrunner2001234-61">[38]</a></sup> All were above average intelligence, several considerably.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[39]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_defendants_at_Nuremberg_Trials.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/The_defendants_at_Nuremberg_Trials.jpg/250px-The_defendants_at_Nuremberg_Trials.jpg" width="250" height="197" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/The_defendants_at_Nuremberg_Trials.jpg/375px-The_defendants_at_Nuremberg_Trials.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fe/The_defendants_at_Nuremberg_Trials.jpg 2x" data-file-width="469" data-file-height="370" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_defendants_at_Nuremberg_Trials.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Defendants listening to translated evidence through headphones</div>

<td>Ribbentrop, Joachim von</td>
<td>129</td>
</tr>

<td>Rosenberg, Alfred</td>
<td>127</td>
</tr>

<td>Sauckel, Fritz</td>
<td>118</td>

<td>Streicher, Julius</td>

<p>Throughout the trials, specifically between January and July 1946, the defendants and a number of <a href="/wiki/Witness" title="Witness">witnesses</a> were interviewed by American psychiatrist <a href="/wiki/Leon_Goldensohn" title="Leon Goldensohn">Leon Goldensohn</a>. His notes detailing the demeanor and comments of the defendants survive; they were edited into book form and published in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldensohn2004_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldensohn2004-65">[42]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jean_Delay" title="Jean Delay">Jean Delay</a> was the psychiatric expert for the French delegation in the trial of <a href="/wiki/Rudolph_Hess" class="mw-redirect" title="Rudolph Hess">Rudolph Hess</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview_of_the_trial">Overview of the trial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg_trials&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Overview of the trial">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Goering_on_trial_(color).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Goering_on_trial_%28color%29.jpg/220px-Goering_on_trial_%28color%29.jpg" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Goering_on_trial_%28color%29.jpg/330px-Goering_on_trial_%28color%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Goering_on_trial_%28color%29.jpg/440px-Goering_on_trial_%28color%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="472" /></a>
